CC   -!- FUNCTION: Forms pores that allow passive diffusion of small
CC       molecules across the outer membrane. It is also a receptor for the
CC       bacteriophage T2. {ECO:0000269|PubMed:19721064}.
CC   -!- SUBUNIT: Homotrimer. {ECO:0000269|PubMed:16079137}.
CC   -!- INTERACTION:
CC       Self; NbExp=7; IntAct=EBI-371336, EBI-371336;
CC       P08083:cna (xeno); NbExp=3; IntAct=EBI-371336, EBI-15691934;
CC       P09883:col (xeno); NbExp=4; IntAct=EBI-371336, EBI-1029888;
CC   -!- SUBCELLULAR LOCATION: Cell outer membrane
CC       {ECO:0000269|PubMed:16079137}; Multi-pass membrane protein
CC       {ECO:0000269|PubMed:16079137}.
CC   -!- INDUCTION: Levels of OmpF protein decrease in a lon/ycgE double
CC       disruption (at protein level). {ECO:0000269|PubMed:19721064}.
CC   -!- DISRUPTION PHENOTYPE: Leads to decreased susceptibility to a
CC       number of hydrophilic antibiotics including ampicillin, cefoxitin
CC       and tetracycline. {ECO:0000269|PubMed:19721064}.
CC   -!- SIMILARITY: Belongs to the Gram-negative porin family.
CC       {ECO:0000305}.

RP   X-RAY CRYSTALLOGRAPHY (4.1 ANGSTROMS) OF 2-283, AND STRUCTURE BY NMR.
RX   PubMed=18832158; DOI=10.1073/pnas.0808115105;
RA   Bayrhuber M., Meins T., Habeck M., Becker S., Giller K., Villinger S.,
RA   Vonrhein C., Griesinger C., Zweckstetter M., Zeth K.;
RT   "Structure of the human voltage-dependent anion channel.";

RN   [43]
RP   STRUCTURE BY NMR, FUNCTION, INTERACTION WITH BCL2L1, AND NADH-BINDING.
RX   PubMed=18755977; DOI=10.1126/science.1161302;
RA   Hiller S., Garces R.G., Malia T.J., Orekhov V.Y., Colombini M.,
RA   Wagner G.;
RT   "Solution structure of the integral human membrane protein VDAC-1 in
RT   detergent micelles.";
RL   Science 321:1206-1210(2008).
CC   -!- FUNCTION: Forms a channel through the mitochondrial outer membrane
CC       and also the plasma membrane. The channel at the outer
CC       mitochondrial membrane allows diffusion of small hydrophilic
CC       molecules; in the plasma membrane it is involved in cell volume
CC       regulation and apoptosis. It adopts an open conformation at low or
CC       zero membrane potential and a closed conformation at potentials
CC       above 30-40 mV. The open state has a weak anion selectivity
CC       whereas the closed state is cation-selective (PubMed:11845315,
CC       PubMed:18755977, PubMed:20230784, PubMed:8420959). May participate
CC       in the formation of the permeability transition pore complex
CC       (PTPC) responsible for the release of mitochondrial products that
CC       triggers apoptosis (PubMed:15033708, PubMed:25296756).
CC       {ECO:0000269|PubMed:11845315, ECO:0000269|PubMed:15033708,
CC       ECO:0000269|PubMed:18755977, ECO:0000269|PubMed:20230784,
CC       ECO:0000269|PubMed:25296756, ECO:0000269|PubMed:8420959}.
CC   -!- ENZYME REGULATION: Inhibited by nitric oxide.
CC       {ECO:0000269|PubMed:21156174}.
CC   -!- SUBUNIT: Interacts with hexokinases including HK1 (PubMed:8420959,
CC       PubMed:22304920). The HK1-VDAC1 complex interacts with ATF2
CC       (PubMed:22304920). Interacts with BCL2L1 (PubMed:18755977,
CC       PubMed:25296756). Interacts with BAK1 (PubMed:25296756). Interacts
CC       with RTL10/BOP (via BH3 domain) (PubMed:23055042). Interacts with
CC       amyloid-beta and APP; induces VDAC1 dephosphorylation
CC       (PubMed:25168729). Component of the mitochondrial permeability
CC       transition pore complex (mPTPC), at least composed of SPG7, VDAC1
CC       and PPIF (PubMed:26387735). Interacts with SPG7, NIPSNAP2 and
CC       SLC25A30 (PubMed:26387735). {ECO:0000269|PubMed:18755977,
CC       ECO:0000269|PubMed:22304920, ECO:0000269|PubMed:23055042,
CC       ECO:0000269|PubMed:25168729, ECO:0000269|PubMed:25296756,
CC       ECO:0000269|PubMed:26387735, ECO:0000269|PubMed:8420959}.
CC   -!- SUBUNIT: (Microbial infection) Interacts with influenza A virus
CC       PB1-F2 protein. {ECO:0000269|PubMed:16201016}.
CC   -!- INTERACTION:
CC       Self; NbExp=4; IntAct=EBI-354158, EBI-354158;
CC       P19367:HK1; NbExp=2; IntAct=EBI-354158, EBI-713162;
CC       Q14643:ITPR1; NbExp=3; IntAct=EBI-354158, EBI-465548;
CC       Q7L3V2:RTL10; NbExp=2; IntAct=EBI-354158, EBI-10697720;
CC   -!- SUBCELLULAR LOCATION: Mitochondrion outer membrane
CC       {ECO:0000269|PubMed:7539795}; Multi-pass membrane protein
CC       {ECO:0000269|PubMed:18755977, ECO:0000269|PubMed:18832158}. Cell
CC       membrane {ECO:0000269|PubMed:25168729,
CC       ECO:0000269|PubMed:25296756}; Multi-pass membrane protein
CC       {ECO:0000269|PubMed:18755977, ECO:0000269|PubMed:18832158}.
CC       Membrane raft {ECO:0000269|PubMed:25168729}; Multi-pass membrane
CC       protein {ECO:0000269|PubMed:18755977,
CC       ECO:0000269|PubMed:18832158}.
CC   -!- TISSUE SPECIFICITY: Heart, liver and skeletal muscle.
CC   -!- DOMAIN: Consists mainly of a membrane-spanning beta-barrel formed
CC       by 19 beta-strands. The helical N-terminus folds back into the
CC       pore opening and plays a role in voltage-gated channel activity.
CC   -!- PTM: Phosphorylation at Ser-193 by NEK1 promotes the open
CC       conformational state preventing excessive mitochondrial membrane
CC       permeability and subsequent apoptotic cell death after injury.
CC       Phosphorylation by the AKT-GSK3B axis stabilizes the protein
CC       probably by preventing ubiquitin-mediated proteasomal degradation.
CC       {ECO:0000269|PubMed:20230784}.
CC   -!- PTM: Ubiquitinated by PRKN during mitophagy, leading to its
CC       degradation and enhancement of mitophagy. Deubiquitinated by
CC       USP30. {ECO:0000269|PubMed:25621951}.
CC   -!- SIMILARITY: Belongs to the eukaryotic mitochondrial porin family.
CC       {ECO:0000305}.

CC       and Haematology;

CC   -!- FUNCTION: Voltage-dependent rectifying anion channel that
CC       facilitates the translocation between chloroplast and cytoplasm of
CC       phosphorylated carbohydrates such as triosephosphate, 3-
CC       phosphoglycerate and inorganic phosphate (Pi) depending of ATP to
CC       triosephosphate ratio in the plastidial intermembrane space; in

CC   -!- FUNCTION: Forms a channel through the mitochondrial outer membrane
CC       that allows diffusion of small hydrophilic molecules. The channel
CC       adopts an open conformation at low or zero membrane potential and
CC       a closed conformation at potentials above 30-40 mV. The open state
CC       has a weak anion selectivity whereas the closed state is cation-
CC       selective.
CC   -!- SUBUNIT: Interacts with hexokinases. {ECO:0000250}.
CC   -!- INTERACTION:
CC       Q96A26:FAM162A; NbExp=2; IntAct=EBI-354022, EBI-6123466;
CC   -!- SUBCELLULAR LOCATION: Mitochondrion outer membrane
CC       {ECO:0000269|PubMed:7539795}.
CC   -!- ALTERNATIVE PRODUCTS:
CC       Event=Alternative splicing; Named isoforms=3;
CC       Name=3;
CC         IsoId=P45880-3; Sequence=Displayed;
CC       Name=1;
CC         IsoId=P45880-1; Sequence=VSP_005077;
CC         Note=Ref.1 (AAA60144) sequence differs from that shown due to a
CC         frameshift in position 303. {ECO:0000305};
CC       Name=2;
CC         IsoId=P45880-2; Sequence=VSP_005076;
CC         Note=Ref.1 (AAA60145) sequence differs from that shown due to a
CC         frameshift in position 277. {ECO:0000305};
CC   -!- TISSUE SPECIFICITY: Expressed in all tissues examined.
CC   -!- DOMAIN: Consists mainly of a membrane-spanning beta-barrel formed
CC       by 19 beta-strands. {ECO:0000250}.
CC   -!- PTM: Ubiquitinated by PRKN during mitophagy, leading to its
CC       degradation and enhancement of mitophagy. Deubiquitinated by
CC       USP30. {ECO:0000269|PubMed:25621951}.
CC   -!- SIMILARITY: Belongs to the eukaryotic mitochondrial porin family.
CC       {ECO:0000305}.

CC   -!- FUNCTION: Voltage-dependent rectifying anion channel that
CC       facilitates the translocation between chloroplast and cytoplasm of
CC       phosphorylated carbohydrates such as triosephosphate, 3-
CC       phosphoglycerate and inorganic phosphate (Pi) depending of ATP to
CC       triosephosphate ratio in the plastidial intermembrane space; in
CC       high triosephosphate/ATP conditions (e.g. photosynthesis), export
CC       of triosphophate from chloroplast (outward rectifying channels),
CC       but in high ATP/triosephosphate conditions (e.g. dark phase),
CC       import of phosphosolutes (inward rectifying channels) (By
CC       similarity). {ECO:0000250}.
CC   -!- SUBCELLULAR LOCATION: Plastid, etioplast membrane {ECO:0000250};
CC       Multi-pass membrane protein {ECO:0000250}. Plastid, chloroplast
CC       outer membrane {ECO:0000250}; Multi-pass membrane protein
CC       {ECO:0000250}. Note=Present in non-green root plastids.
CC       {ECO:0000250}.
CC   -!- SIMILARITY: Belongs to the plastid outer envelope porin OEP21 (TC
CC       1.B.29) family. {ECO:0000305}.

CC   -!- FUNCTION: Forms a channel through the mitochondrial outer membrane
CC       that allows diffusion of small hydrophilic molecules. The channel
CC       adopts an open conformation at low or zero membrane potential and
CC       a closed conformation at potentials above 30-40 mV. The open state
CC       has a weak anion selectivity whereas the closed state is cation-
CC       selective (By similarity). {ECO:0000250|UniProtKB:P45880}.
CC   -!- SUBUNIT: Interacts with hexokinases.
CC       {ECO:0000250|UniProtKB:P45880}.
CC   -!- SUBCELLULAR LOCATION: Mitochondrion outer membrane
CC       {ECO:0000250|UniProtKB:P45880}.
CC   -!- DOMAIN: Consists mainly of a membrane-spanning beta-barrel formed
CC       by 19 beta-strands. {ECO:0000250|UniProtKB:P21796}.
CC   -!- PTM: Ubiquitinated by PRKN during mitophagy, leading to its
CC       degradation and enhancement of mitophagy. Deubiquitinated by
CC       USP30. {ECO:0000250|UniProtKB:P45880}.
CC   -!- SIMILARITY: Belongs to the eukaryotic mitochondrial porin family.
CC       {ECO:0000255}.

CC   -!- FUNCTION: Involved in the active translocation of vitamin B12
CC       (cyanocobalamin) across the outer membrane to the periplasmic
CC       space. It derives its energy for transport by interacting with the
CC       trans-periplasmic membrane protein TonB. Is also a receptor for
CC       bacteriophages BF23 and C1, and for A and E colicins.
CC       {ECO:0000269|PubMed:10485884, ECO:0000269|PubMed:2687240,
CC       ECO:0000269|PubMed:2982793}.
CC   -!- ENZYME REGULATION: Calcium increases vitamin B12 binding affinity
CC       by a factor of 50-100. {ECO:0000269|PubMed:14499604}.
CC   -!- SUBUNIT: Interacts with TonB. {ECO:0000269|PubMed:10485884,
CC       ECO:0000269|PubMed:14528295}.
CC   -!- SUBCELLULAR LOCATION: Cell outer membrane
CC       {ECO:0000269|PubMed:12595710, ECO:0000269|PubMed:12652322,
CC       ECO:0000269|PubMed:2687240, ECO:0000269|PubMed:2982793}; Multi-
CC       pass membrane protein {ECO:0000269|PubMed:12595710,
CC       ECO:0000269|PubMed:12652322, ECO:0000269|PubMed:2687240,
CC       ECO:0000269|PubMed:2982793}.
CC   -!- INDUCTION: Constitutively expressed. Primary control of btuB
CC       expression by cobalamin occurs at the level of translation
CC       initiation. {ECO:0000269|PubMed:9852020}.
CC   -!- SIMILARITY: Belongs to the TonB-dependent receptor family. BtuB
CC       (TC 1.B.14.3.1) subfamily. {ECO:0000255|HAMAP-Rule:MF_01531,
CC       ECO:0000305}.

CC   -!- FUNCTION: Voltage-dependent rectifying anion channel that
CC       facilitates the translocation between chloroplast and cytoplasm of
CC       phosphorylated carbohydrates such as triosephosphate, 3-
CC       phosphoglycerate and inorganic phosphate (Pi) depending of ATP to
CC       triosephosphate ratio in the plastidial intermembrane space; in
CC       high triosephosphate/ATP conditions (e.g. photosynthesis), export
CC       of triosphophate from chloroplast (outward rectifying channels),
CC       but in high ATP/triosephosphate conditions (e.g. dark phase),
CC       import of phosphosolutes (inward rectifying channels) (By
CC       similarity). {ECO:0000250}.

RA   Samol I., Rossig C., Buhr F., Springer A., Pollmann S., Lahroussi A.,

CC   -!- FUNCTION: Voltage-dependent high-conductance channel with a
CC       slightly cation-selectivity; selective for amino acids but
CC       excludes triosephosphates or uncharged sugars (By similarity).
CC       Non-essential amino acid-selective channel protein and
CC       translocation pore for NADPH:protochlorophyllide oxidoreductase A
CC       (PORA) and possibly PORB. Involved in PORA precursor (pPORA)
CC       import and thus confers photoprotection onto etiolated seedlings
CC       during greening. {ECO:0000250, ECO:0000269|PubMed:14769929,
CC       ECO:0000269|PubMed:17202255, ECO:0000269|PubMed:17261815,
CC       ECO:0000269|PubMed:19567834, ECO:0000269|PubMed:21098556,
CC       ECO:0000269|PubMed:21098557}.
CC   -!- ENZYME REGULATION: Stimulated by GTP.
CC       {ECO:0000269|PubMed:15773849}.
CC   -!- SUBUNIT: Homodimer and oligomers in membrane (By similarity).
CC       Forms large complexes including TOC33, pPORA and OEP161 during
CC       pPORA import into plastids at the plastid envelope membrane.
CC       {ECO:0000250}.
CC   -!- SUBCELLULAR LOCATION: Plastid, chloroplast outer membrane; Multi-
CC       pass membrane protein. Plastid, etioplast membrane; Multi-pass
CC       membrane protein.
CC   -!- TISSUE SPECIFICITY: Expressed predominantly in leaves and
CC       cotyledons. {ECO:0000269|PubMed:16709189,
CC       ECO:0000269|PubMed:17202255}.
CC   -!- INDUCTION: Transient reduction upon de-etiolation (illuminated 5-
CC       day-old etiolated seedlings) (at protein level). Strongly induced
CC       by low-temperature stress and weakly in response to osmotic
CC       stress, salicylic acid (SA) and exogenous abscisic acid (ABA)
CC       treatments. {ECO:0000269|PubMed:16709189,
CC       ECO:0000269|PubMed:21098556}.
CC   -!- DISRUPTION PHENOTYPE: Strong red Pchlide fluorescence after 3.5-4
CC       days of growth in the dark, and cell death after subsequent
CC       illumination. Conditional seedling lethal phenotype related to
CC       defects in import and assembly of NADPH:protochlorophyllide
CC       (Pchlide) oxidoreductase A; excess Pchlide accumulated in the dark
CC       operates as photosensitizer and provokes cell death during
CC       greening. {ECO:0000269|PubMed:17261815,
CC       ECO:0000269|PubMed:19567834, ECO:0000269|PubMed:21098556,
CC       ECO:0000269|PubMed:21098557}.
CC   -!- SIMILARITY: Belongs to the Tim17/Tim22/Tim23 family. Plastid outer
CC       envelope porin OEP16 (TC 1.B.30) subfamily. {ECO:0000305}.

CC   -!- FUNCTION: Catalyzes the cleavage of sphingomyelin, a major lipid
CC       in eukaryotic cells, into ceramide and phosphocholine, which are
CC       then utilized by M.bovis as carbon, nitrogen and phosphorus
CC       sources, respectively. Thus, enables M.bovis to utilize
CC       sphingomyelin as a source of several essential nutrients for
CC       intracellular growth during infection. Furthermore, lyses
CC       erythrocytes and constitutes a hemolytic factor.
CC       {ECO:0000250|UniProtKB:P9WKQ1}.
CC   -!- CATALYTIC ACTIVITY: Sphingomyelin + H(2)O = N-acylsphingosine +
CC       phosphocholine. {ECO:0000250|UniProtKB:P9WKQ1}.
CC   -!- SUBCELLULAR LOCATION: Cell outer membrane
CC       {ECO:0000250|UniProtKB:P9WKQ1}; Multi-pass membrane protein
CC       {ECO:0000250|UniProtKB:P9WKQ1}.
CC   -!- DOMAIN: Consists of a surface-exposed C-terminal sphingomyelinase
CC       domain and a putative outer membrane-spanning N-terminal channel
CC       domain able to mediate glucose and phosphocholine uptake across
CC       the outer membrane. {ECO:0000250|UniProtKB:P9WKQ1}.
